        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122141565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5786897079375676316">This book was beyond fantastic. Fantastic, but also painful.<br/><br/>About a third of the way through I had to stop reading with the realisation that this book was going to break my heart. It was going to be one of those ones that left me feeling like my emotions had been thrown into a blender and left me torn to shreds. I wasn't wrong and while a part of me did want to go hide in my bed listening to happy music to escape the pain of the story, I just had to finish it.<br/><br/>I figured out what the plot twists w</span>
  <span id="freeText5786897079375676316" style="display:none">This book was beyond fantastic. Fantastic, but also painful.<br /><br />About a third of the way through I had to stop reading with the realisation that this book was going to break my heart. It was going to be one of those ones that left me feeling like my emotions had been thrown into a blender and left me torn to shreds. I wasn't wrong and while a part of me did want to go hide in my bed listening to happy music to escape the pain of the story, I just had to finish it.<br /><br />I figured out what the plot twists were going to be early on (all except for one), but I hoped I was wrong and I was turning the pages with dread because I didn't want to be bawling my eyes out when one of the things finally happened - I felt like Grace.<br /><br />It was really intense - and it felt sort of masochistic reading it, because it literally hurt, Grace's pain felt so real to me and when I was finished reading the book, I walked around in an Entangled induced daze for a few hours and literally the first thing I said was, "Stupid book, tearing me to pieces!" to my best friend because that's how it felt. Ten days later and the book is still getting to me.<br /><br />Now, a book having that effect on me is a sign of how its brilliance, there aren't many that get under my skin like that but this one did and I wanted to email Cat and say, "Why? WHY would you do that to me? To Grace? I demand a sequel filled with rainbows and butterflies to make up for it!"... of course, I didn’t because it was the hurt that made the book so great, it was like -- the art was in the agony. <br /><br />Books are often an escape, but for me this one wasn't - it was raw and intense and real and I absolutely love it for that... and I hate it for that too. I don't think I'll ever be able to reread it - and that is a compliment to the author, really. Some books worm their way into your heart and under your skin and you just know they're going to stick with you. This is one of them... but reading it hurt and rereading it would be too painful but it has definitely earned it’s place on my all time favourite books shelf.<br /><br />It was like reading about everything about life that hurts and I dunno, sometimes I just need that in a book. If this book isn’t on your wish list, then add it, seriously.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5786897079375676316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5048720391785609310"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534637347i/26153355.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Cat Clarke knows the teenage girl inside out. She seems to have a sense of some of the feelings behind self harm. Her exploring suicide could have been powerful. It really could have. But I have no idea whatsoever what she was hoping to achieve with <i>Entangled</i> besides book sales.<br/><br/>There's nothing novel about a book in which someone in a <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[coma is dreaming <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I hate that the whole thing was made about relationship drama with virtually no exploration of Grace's father <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view</a></span>
  <span id="freeText5048720391785609310" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534637347i/26153355.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Cat Clarke knows the teenage girl inside out. She seems to have a sense of some of the feelings behind self harm. Her exploring suicide could have been powerful. It really could have. But I have no idea whatsoever what she was hoping to achieve with <i>Entangled</i> besides book sales.<br><br>There's nothing novel about a book in which someone in a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[coma is dreaming <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I hate that the whole thing was made about relationship drama with virtually no exploration of Grace's father <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[killing himself <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. There's almost no time given for the heroine to consider this as a factor. She's too busy telling us about her love life. But hey, what do I know? I only had a friend kill himself after another friend's suicide. We're told right at the end that Grace's friend was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[raped <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Her mother <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[decides to pull together and parent <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. These things are all huge. Or they should be. But they're capped by two boys being there for her, one of whom isn't even <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[real <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br>It is so important that we talk about suicide that I can't help but feel this almost as a personal affront. I know many people that read YA aren't necessarily teenagers but it is ultimately aimed at potentially impressionable young people and I feel that authors writing for this age bracket have a responsibility to give their readers space to thoroughly explore sensitive issues they raise, even if only through a Q&amp;A at the end. I think it would be all too easy to take away the message from <i>Entangled</i> that if you attempt suicide your friends will suddenly start being honest with you and you might get a new boyfriend if one feels sorry for you. This is trite and cheap.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Savannah (Books With Bite)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Savannah (Books With Bite)" href="/user/show/3381656-savannah-books-with-bite">Savannah (Books With Bite)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154720886" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4364798090264312472">For some reason, and I don't know why, I thought this was a paranormal book. It wasn't. Instead it was a great book that captured me, that I had to keep on reading till the very end. It enslaved my soul, sucking me to the bottomless pit of doom. Yes, this book had lots of drama in it that it left me with a book hangover.<br/><br/>The storyline is filled with a secret, betrayals, and a love lost. I can say I enjoyed this book very much, but sometimes the drama got to me. I just felt like going into the boo</span>
  <span id="freeText4364798090264312472" style="display:none">For some reason, and I don't know why, I thought this was a paranormal book. It wasn't. Instead it was a great book that captured me, that I had to keep on reading till the very end. It enslaved my soul, sucking me to the bottomless pit of doom. Yes, this book had lots of drama in it that it left me with a book hangover.<br /><br />The storyline is filled with a secret, betrayals, and a love lost. I can say I enjoyed this book very much, but sometimes the drama got to me. I just felt like going into the book opening the characters life and slapping them. Then again, the book was engaging enough that you held on listening to every secret told, every betrayal exposed and a heart breaking.<br /><br />The characters themselves were just whacked out. They were horrible people to each other. I mean, some of things they did made me think, why even bother? Move on! Then again, the characters created enough drama to last me a lifetime.<br /><br />What I liked about this book is the main character, Grace. The author, Ms. Clarke did a great job creating a character with flaws. This character was messed up from the very beginning till the end. She could only take so much. So much has happened in her life its no wonder she acted and did the things she did. Grace, I feel, at the end, really learned so much. I can only hope that Grace will see things differently.<br /><br />There was lots of sex (implied), cursing, drinking, and cutting. This book is a great book about a girl who goes down the rabbit hole, falling into an oblivion of hell, that I can only hope she can come out of. Not sure what else to say other that this book is filled with so much drama, your head will be spinning.<br /><br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18051147990684388284">Wow, what can I say about Entangled? <br/><br/>Well it's a must read. It's hard going with the 'self harm' aspects which for many books I've read with suicide, self harm etc this was well written. I wasn't left wondering why Grace cut herself, more with an understanding of it all.<br/><br/>I was a little disappointed with the ending, for I wanted to know what happened in the end (I won't go into that here as I don't want to spoil it for others). <br/><br/>I also would liked to have seen more character development with Devon </span>
  <span id="freeText18051147990684388284" style="display:none">Wow, what can I say about Entangled? <br /><br />Well it's a must read. It's hard going with the 'self harm' aspects which for many books I've read with suicide, self harm etc this was well written. I wasn't left wondering why Grace cut herself, more with an understanding of it all.<br /><br />I was a little disappointed with the ending, for I wanted to know what happened in the end (I won't go into that here as I don't want to spoil it for others). <br /><br />I also would liked to have seen more character development with Devon and Grace for I feel they were more alike than what lead me to think. Nate was a great character, I liked how he was bought into the story and I was also left feeling sorry for Sal.<br /><br />I wanted to help the characters even when I could see what was happening. May I also add what a fantastic way to open the book too with Grace and her predicament.<br /><br />Cat Clarke has really hit the nail on the head, read in one day over 2 sittings; I didn't want to put this book down but had to stop to eat my dinner! I really do recomend this book to others. It can be hard to read in places but with such strong characters and a great leading voice from Grace I thought it truly deserved its 5 stars!<br /><br />Review also featured on my blog - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bewitchedbooks.co.uk/">http://www.bewitchedbooks.co.uk/</a></span>

<div id="review_172902341" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172902341" />
    <a title="Antonia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5548487-antonia"><img alt="Antonia" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172902341?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Antonia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Antonia" href="/user/show/5548487-antonia">Antonia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548487-antonia?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548487-antonia?shelf=it-s-okay-ish">it-s-okay-ish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer172902341&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172902341" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16422621991475042435">There were two reasons why I bought this book. <br/>1) The cover was stunning, absolutely beautiful. Even though they say that you should never judge a book by it's cover I just couldn't help it.<br/>2) I had heard about this book before and the premise was excellent. I loved the mystery behind the whole 'kidnapped in a room with only pens and paper' thing. I was really looking forward to discovering what was happening and as a result of that I finished the book in one sitting. <br/>and 3) I know this doesn't </span>
  <span id="freeText16422621991475042435" style="display:none">There were two reasons why I bought this book. <br />1) The cover was stunning, absolutely beautiful. Even though they say that you should never judge a book by it's cover I just couldn't help it.<br />2) I had heard about this book before and the premise was excellent. I loved the mystery behind the whole 'kidnapped in a room with only pens and paper' thing. I was really looking forward to discovering what was happening and as a result of that I finished the book in one sitting. <br />and 3) I know this doesn't actually count as a reason but I have a pet cat called Clarkie. :) <br /><br />Well, I have to say that I was disappointed unfortunately. It was ok, but not great. I can understand that some people adored the book, the countless sweet moments and the "supposedly" big twist at the end but I can also understand how people hated it. A girl at 17, whiny, suicidal, a drunk, cuts herself, sleeps with anyone etc, it can be very hard to read for some people. Personally though, I don't have a problem with the main character, Grace, as there are actual people who are like that in the real world. Clarke just wanted someone like that in her story, and to be honest she is quite a spunky character, (she has 'Eeyore' pajamas :D ) so who is to complain? <br /><br />But, ignoring the characters for now I was really disappointed with the plot line that promised so much and never delivered. I wished so much that Clarke would surprise me with something brilliant and awe-inspiring but in actual fact it was just so cliche that I nearly cried. I knew that Nat and Sal, her boyfriend and best friend, were sleeping together since 1/4 of the way in, (lets face it, Clarke was dropping hints on nearly every page) but for the actual whole white room to be a dream. Come on Clarke, surely you could have done better than that. <br />Even if Grace was kidnapped and she just ended up escaping from this weird creep I would have been happier. Oh well, I suppose we can't all have what we want. <br /><br />Another thing that drove me crazy was her mother. Nearly every book out their is about some neglected teen whose parents hate them or are never around. I would have preferred the mother to be someone who cares too much and then Grace had to sneak out, or for Clarke to even give more depth about her mother. Like for the readers to see her mourning the loss of her husband, so she doesn't seem like such a heartless person who sleeps with her husbands best friend (ie. Uncle Mick)<br /><br />I don't feel that much towards Ethan, He was a figment of her imagination after all so I don't have much to say about him. However I would just like to say that I loved Sal as a character, and Nat. Loads of people probably hate them for being such B****s to Grace but in my eyes it seemed like one of those situations that couldn't be helped. They liked each other and cared for each other but Grace seemed to get all 'Entangled' into something she shouldn't have. (Pardon the pun, a way too overused phrase) Which wasn't her fault by the way. I just see Grace as an unfortunate victim. If it was set in the eyes of Sal or Nat, Grace would definitely be the bad guy so I can't complain about any of them.<br /><br />So, over all Entangled wasn't great. Yes I won't give it a bad review because it did shine in some places. For instance I couldn't help but smile at some of the sweet moments and cheesy jokes and this book really did interest me when i saw it. But it definitely doesn't deserve full stars, as somehow it wasn't what I was expecting. It didn't give me something original or completely mind blowing so I guess I can't say that I enjoyed it. Yes it was funny, Yes it was sweet, but I can't say Yes, this book is amazing. <br />xx</span>
  <a data-text-id="16422621991475042435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_291408190" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/291408190" />
    <a title="Rachel S" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5806907-rachel-s"><img alt="Rachel S" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603640746p2/5806907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/291408190?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel S" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel S" href="/user/show/5806907-rachel-s">Rachel S</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer291408190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18080386738548761495">Ooooh, I have so much to say about this book I don't even know where to begin... I am very glad that I finally got around to reading it because I must say, this is a book no avid reader should miss! It has everything from a great writing style to well planned characters and even faces some of the most troubling issues facing teenagers today.<br/><br/>This plot was so... well planned out and developed and relatable. So different. It kept me guessing throughout. Some twists did surprise me and even though o</span>
  <span id="freeText18080386738548761495" style="display:none">Ooooh, I have so much to say about this book I don't even know where to begin... I am very glad that I finally got around to reading it because I must say, this is a book no avid reader should miss! It has everything from a great writing style to well planned characters and even faces some of the most troubling issues facing teenagers today.<br /><br />This plot was so... well planned out and developed and relatable. So different. It kept me guessing throughout. Some twists did surprise me and even though one of the biggest twists I sort-of guessed a little about, certain parts in the story kept making me doubt myself.<br /><br />Clarke's writing style was just perfect for this story. It was so utterly believable that it was a teenager and Grace's character was potrayed absolutely perfectly because it was being told through her eyes. Even though at the start I had mixed feelings about the swearing and the general relationship involvement, as the story progressed I realised that was just who Grace was and that she had come to be that way because of all the tragic situations she'd been through. For most part I was ready to give this book a rating of four but when the story started toward the end and was so skillfully tied up I just knew it was a five star rating for sure!<br /><br />I would also really like to talk about the issues faced in this book. Clarke has so thoughtfully showed what some troubled teens can experience. Through Grace we realise that most people do what they do (for example: drinking) for a reason. Maybe they have went through something traumatic and find it easier to feel pain than to actually face themselves and their own "messed-up" lives. Like Grace.<br /><br />Oh, Grace. Poor, poor, Grace (even though she probably wouldn't appreciate my pity)! Despite the swearing and the drinking and such I actually found her quite a great main character. I just felt so sorry for what she has had to suffer through. She is generally a zoomed in version of a rebellious teen with so much more to her than what she gives herself credit for. Sometimes I just wanted to shake her so she would stop or listen but mostly I just really wanted to be there for her!<br /><br />The other characters I'd like to mention are Sal and Nat. I'll start with Sal. Now that I've finished reading the book I really want to scream at her for blaming and pratically using Grace. When I was more naive at the beginning I actually found her an okay character but now that I know the whole story I really don't like her one eensey little bit. I can't believe what she did to Grace. She was supposed to be her best friend but what she done was despicable - and messed-up! Woah, I've never had that strong a feeling against any character before - and I'm not even on to Nat! But I suppose I should start now.<br /><br />I thought Nat was going to be one of those more-than-meets-the-eye but still with the normal teenage boy in him character but now that I've finished the book, like I did with Sal, my feelings changed and I hate him! I actually wanted to slap him after I turned the last page, but since I couldn't do that I sort of punched the book instead hehe. Urghhh, I can't even talk about him without sizzling!<br /><br />The ending. Oh, the ending! I can't believe it left on a cliff hanger. I just need to know what happens! If only a few more chapters, or a sequel! ... I just really hope Grace doesn't forgive Sal and Nat!<br /><br />Overall I found Entangled a really thought-provoking and enjoyable book. I managed to read it quite quickly because I was always wanting to know what was going to happen. I definetly think you should check out this book if you are looking for one powerful read!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18080386738548761495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

		<td>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OFGU6mAkVCOuKTP1w2D0oGOhS0IZOLBvwk9AUbfPSbPUHdoh6KBBrjoBUxBJVbWTuz12wfJddFusKBNzyWDU4g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lzi1fF9OufMMpBQycRF3xQ1aiLzdzBCeAH8RmoJWWgB7dPu318qsfpiMdNf7JDb21ca1Pzap1KpuGEK4/PnHUQ==')})
  }
//]]>

She likes cheese A LOT, especially baked camembert.</span>
